Cet article concerne l'empire. Pour le califat associé, voir [Califat ottoman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Caliphate "Califat ottoman") .

src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/d/d2/Blank.png" width="22" height="15"></span></span></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>

L' **Empire ottoman** <sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">[</font></font></span><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> l </font></font><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">]</font></font></span></a></sup> ( [/ ˈ ɒ t ə m ə n /](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Aide : API/anglais") <sup class="ext-phonos-attribution noexcerpt navigation-not-searchable"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:LL-Q1860_(eng)-Flame,_not_lame-ottoman.wav" title="Fichier:LL-Q1860 (eng)-Flamme, pas boiteux-ottoman.wav"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">ⓘ</font></font></a></sup> ), également appelé l'**Empire turc**, <sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> [</font></font></span><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> 24</font></font><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> ] </font></font></span></a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">[</font></font></span><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> 25</font></font><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> ]</font></font></span></a></sup> était un[royaume impérial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire "Empire") <sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> [</font></font></span><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> m</font></font><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> ]</font></font></span></a></sup> qui contrôlait une grande partie de[l'Europe du Sud-Est](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Europe "Europe du Sud-Est"),[de l'Asie occidentale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Asia "Asie de l'Ouest")et[de l'Afrique du Nord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Africa "Afrique du Nord")du 14e au début du 20e siècle ; il contrôlait également des parties du sud-est[de l'Europe centrale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Europe "Europe Centrale"), entre le début du 16e et le début du 18e siècle. <sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> [</font></font></span><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> 26</font></font><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> ] </font></font></span></a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">[</font></font></span><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> 27</font></font><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> ] </font></font></span></a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">[</font></font></span><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> 28</font></font><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> ]</font></font></span></a></sup>

L'empire est né d'un [*beylik*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolian_beyliks "Beyliks anatoliens") , ou [principauté](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principality "Principauté") , fondé dans le nord-ouest  de [l'Anatolie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolia "Anatolie") vers 1299 par le chef tribal [turkmène](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkoman_\(ethnonym\) "Turkoman (ethnonym)") [Osman Ier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_I "Osman I") . Ses successeurs [conquirent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe "Ottoman wars in Europe") une grande partie de l'Anatolie et s'étendirent aux [Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkans "Balkans") au milieu du XIVe siècle, transformant leur [petit royaume](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petty_kingdom "Petty kingdom") en un empire transcontinental. Les Ottomans mirent fin à l' [Empire byzantin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire") avec la [conquête de Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople "Fall of Constantinople") en 1453 par [Mehmed II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmed_II "Mehmed II") . Avec sa capitale à [Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Istanbul#Ottoman_Empire "History of Istanbul") (aujourd'hui [Istanbul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul") ) et contrôlant une partie importante du [bassin méditerranéen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin "Mediterranean Basin") , l'Empire ottoman fut au cœur des interactions entre le [Moyen-Orient](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East "Middle East") et l'Europe pendant six siècles. Régnant sur de nombreux peuples, l'empire accorda divers niveaux d'autonomie à ses nombreuses communautés confessionnelles, ou *[millets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Millet_\(Ottoman_Empire\) "Millet (Ottoman Empire)")* , pour gérer leurs propres affaires conformément à [la loi islamique](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_law "Islamic law") . Sous les règnes de [Sélim Ier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selim_I "Selim I") et [de Soliman le Magnifique](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent "Suleiman the Magnificent") , l'Empire ottoman devint une [puissance mondiale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_power "Global power") . <sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">[</font></span></a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-42"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> 29 </font></a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">]</font></span></a></sup> "Turkmène (ethnonyme)")* "Millet (Empire ottoman)")*<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"></font></span><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"></font><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"></font></span></a></sup>

Alors que l'on pensait autrefois que l'Empire ottoman était entré dans une [période de déclin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Decline_Thesis "Thèse du déclin ottoman") après la mort de Soliman le Magnifique, le consensus académique moderne postule que l'empire a continué à maintenir une économie, une société et une armée flexibles et fortes pendant une grande partie du XVIIIe siècle. Les Ottomans ont subi des défaites militaires à la fin du XVIIIe et au début du XIXe siècle, culminant avec la [perte de territoires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decline_and_modernization_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Déclin et modernisation de l'Empire ottoman") . Avec [la montée du nationalisme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rise_of_nationalism_in_the_Ottoman_Empire "La montée du nationalisme dans l'Empire ottoman") , un certain nombre de nouveaux États ont émergé dans les Balkans. Suite aux réformes *[Tanzimat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanzimat "Tanzimat")* au cours du XIXe siècle, l'État ottoman est devenu plus puissant et organisé en interne. Lors de la [révolution de 1876](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1876_Ottoman_Revolution "Révolution ottomane de 1876") , l'Empire ottoman a tenté [une monarchie constitutionnelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Constitutional_Era "Première ère constitutionnelle") , avant de revenir à une dictature royaliste sous [Abdul Hamid II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdul_Hamid_II "Abdul Hamid II") , après la [Grande Crise d'Orient](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Eastern_Crisis "Grande crise de l'Est") .

À la fin du XIXe siècle, les intellectuels ottomans, connus sous le nom de [Jeunes-Turcs,](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Turks "Jeunes Turcs") cherchèrent à libéraliser et à rationaliser la société et la politique selon les principes occidentaux, ce qui aboutit à la [Révolution des Jeunes-Turcs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution "Révolution des Jeunes Turcs") de 1908, menée par le [Comité Union et Progrès](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress "Comité Union et Progrès") (CUP), qui rétablit [une monarchie constitutionnelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era "Deuxième ère constitutionnelle") . Cependant, après les désastreuses [guerres balkaniques](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkan_Wars "Guerres des Balkans") , le CUP se radicalisa et se nationalisa de plus en plus, [menant un coup d'État en 1913](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1913_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "Coup d'État ottoman de 1913") qui instaura une dictature.

Français Aux XIXe et début du XXe siècles, [la persécution des musulmans pendant la contraction ottomane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims_during_the_Ottoman_contraction "Persécution des musulmans pendant la contraction ottomane") et [dans l'Empire russe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#Russian_Empire "Persécution des musulmans") a entraîné des pertes en vies humaines à grande échelle et [une migration massive vers la Turquie actuelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhacir "Muhacir") en provenance des [Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkans "Balkans") , [du Caucase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus "Caucase") et [de Crimée](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_Khanate "Khanat de Crimée") . <sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">[</font></font></span><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> 30 </font></font><span class="cite-bracket"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">]</font></font></span></a></sup> Le CUP a rejoint [la Première Guerre mondiale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "Première Guerre mondiale") aux côtés des [puissances centrales](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers "puissances centrales") . Il a lutté contre la dissidence interne, en particulier la [révolte arabe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Revolt "Révolte arabe") , et s'est engagé dans [un génocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Ottoman_genocides "Génocides ottomans tardifs") contre [les Arméniens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide "génocide arménien") , [les Assyriens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assyrian_genocide "génocide assyrien") et [les Grecs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_genocide "génocide grec") . Au [lendemain de la Première Guerre mondiale , les](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I "Les conséquences de la Première Guerre mondiale") [puissances alliées](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Alliés de la Première Guerre mondiale") victorieuses ont occupé et [partagé](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partition_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Partage de l'Empire ottoman") l'Empire ottoman, qui a perdu ses territoires du sud au profit du [Royaume-Uni et de la France . La](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement "Accord Sykes-Picot") [guerre d'indépendance turque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence "Guerre d'indépendance turque") victorieuse , menée par [Mustafa Kemal Atatürk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk "Mustafa Kemal Atatürk") contre les Alliés occupants, a conduit à l'émergence de la [République de Turquie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turquie") et à l' [abolition de la monarchie ottomane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolition_of_the_Ottoman_sultanate "Abolition du sultanat ottoman") en 1922.

## Étymologie

See also: [Osman I § Name](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_I#Name "Osman I")

The word *Ottoman* is a historical [anglicisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglicisation_\(linguistics\) "Anglicisation (linguistique)") of the name of [Osman I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_I "Osman I"), the founder of the Empire and of the ruling [House of Osman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_dynasty "dynastie ottomane") (also known as the Ottoman dynasty). Osman's name in turn was the Turkish form of the Arabic name *[ʿUthmān](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uthman_\(name\) "Othman (nom)")* (عثمان). In [Ottoman Turkish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish "turc ottoman"), the empire was referred to as *Devlet-i ʿAlīye-yi ʿOsmānīye* (دولت عليه عثمانیه), lit. '**Sublime Ottoman State**', or simply *Devlet-i ʿOsmānīye* (دولت عثمانيه‎), lit. '**Ottoman State**'.

The Turkish word for "Ottoman" (*Osmanlı*) originally referred to the tribal followers of Osman in the fourteenth century. The word subsequently came to be used to refer to the empire's military-administrative elite. In contrast, the term "Turk" (*Türk*) was used to refer to the Anatolian peasant and tribal population and was seen as a disparaging term when applied to urban, educated individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 26">: 26 </span></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In the [early modern period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_modern_period "Période moderne"), an educated, urban-dwelling Turkish speaker who was not a member of the military-administrative class typically referred to themselves neither as an *Osmanlı* nor as a *Türk*, but rather as a *Rūmī* (رومى), or "Roman", meaning an inhabitant of the territory of the former [Byzantine Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Empire byzantin") in the Balkans and Anatolia. The term *Rūmī* was also used to refer to Turkish speakers by the other Muslim peoples of the empire and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 11">: 11 </span></sup> 

In Western Europe, the names Ottoman Empire, Turkish Empire and Turkey were often used interchangeably, with Turkey being increasingly favoured both in formal and informal situations. This dichotomy was officially ended in 1920–1923, when the newly established [Ankara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara "Ankara")\-based [Turkish government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey "Grande Assemblée nationale de Turquie") chose Turkey as the sole official name. At present, most scholarly historians avoid the terms "Turkey", "Turks", and "Turkish" when referring to the Ottomans, due to the empire's multinational character.<sup id="cite_ref-Soucek-2015_47-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Soucek-2015-47"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

## History

Main article: [History of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Histoire de l'Empire ottoman")

See also: [Territorial evolution of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Évolution territoriale de l'Empire ottoman")

### Rise (c. 1299–1453)

Main article: [Rise of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rise_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "L'essor de l'Empire ottoman")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Sultan_Uthman_I.jpg/250px-Sultan_Uthman_I.jpg)

[Ottoman miniature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_miniature "Miniature ottomane") of [Osman I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_I "Osman I") by Yahya Bustanzâde (18th century)

As the [Rum Sultanate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum "Sultanat de Rum") declined in the 13th century, [Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolia "Anatolie") was divided into a patchwork of independent Turkish principalities known as the [Anatolian Beyliks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolian_Beyliks "Beyliks anatoliens"). One of these, in the region of [Bithynia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bithynia "Bithynie") on the frontier of the [Byzantine Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Empire byzantin"), was led by the Turkish<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> tribal leader [Osman I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_I "Osman I") (d. 1323/4),<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> a figure of obscure origins from whom the name Ottoman is derived.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 444">: 444 </span></sup>  Osman's early followers consisted of Turkish tribal groups and Byzantine renegades, with many but not all converts to Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 59">: 59 </span></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 127">: 127 </span></sup>  Osman extended control of his principality by conquering Byzantine towns along the [Sakarya River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sakarya_River "Rivière Sakarya"). A Byzantine defeat at the [Battle of Bapheus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Bapheus "Bataille de Baphée") in 1302 contributed to Osman's rise. It is not well understood how the early Ottomans came to dominate their neighbors, due to the lack of sources surviving. The [Ghaza thesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghaza_thesis "Thèse de Ghaza") popular during the 20th century credited their success to rallying religious warriors to fight for them in the name of [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam"), but it is no longer generally accepted. No other hypothesis has attracted broad acceptance.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 5, 10">: 5, 10 </span></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 104">: 104 </span></sup> 

In the century after Osman I, Ottoman rule had begun to extend over Anatolia and the [Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Balkans "Histoire des Balkans"). The earliest conflicts began during the [Byzantine–Ottoman wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars "Guerres byzantines-ottomanes"), waged in Anatolia in the late 13th century before entering Europe in the mid-14th century, followed by the [Bulgarian–Ottoman wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgarian%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars "Guerres bulgaro-ottomanes") and the [Serbian–Ottoman wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbian%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars "Guerres serbo-ottomanes") in the mid-14th century. Much of this period was characterised by [Ottoman expansion into the Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rumelia "Roumélie"). Osman's son, [Orhan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orhan "Orhan"), captured the northwestern Anatolian city of [Bursa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bursa "Bursa") in 1326, making it the new capital and supplanting Byzantine control in the region. The important port of [Thessaloniki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thessaloniki "Thessalonique") was captured from the [Venetians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Venice "République de Venise") in 1387 and sacked. The Ottoman victory in [Kosovo in 1389](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo "Bataille du Kosovo") effectively marked the [end of Serbian power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_the_Serbian_Empire "Chute de l'Empire serbe") in the region, paving the way for Ottoman expansion into Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 95–96">: 95–96 </span></sup>  The [Battle of Nicopolis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Nicopolis "Bataille de Nicopolis") for the [Bulgarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Bulgarian_Empire "Second Empire bulgare") [Tsardom of Vidin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsardom_of_Vidin "Tsarat de Vidin") in 1396, regarded as the last large-scale [crusade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crusades "Croisades") of the [Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Ages "Moyen-âge"), failed to stop the advance of the victorious Ottomans.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg/250px-Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg)

The [Battle of Nicopolis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Nicopolis "Bataille de Nicopolis") in 1396, as depicted in an [Ottoman miniature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_miniature "Miniature ottomane") from 1523

As the Turks expanded into the Balkans, the [conquest of Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sieges_of_Constantinople#Ottoman_Sieges "Sièges de Constantinople") became a crucial objective. The Ottomans had already wrested control of nearly all former Byzantine lands surrounding the city, but the strong defense of Constantinople's strategic position on the [Bosporus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosporus "Bosphore") Strait made it difficult to conquer. In 1402, the Byzantines were temporarily relieved when the [Turco-Mongol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turco-Mongol "turco-mongol") leader [Timur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timur "Timur"), founder of the [Timurid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timurid_Empire "Empire timouride"), invaded Ottoman Anatolia from the east. In the [Battle of Ankara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Ankara "Bataille d'Ankara") in 1402, Timur defeated Ottoman forces and took Sultan [Bayezid I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayezid_I "Bayezid I") as prisoner, throwing the empire into disorder. The [ensuing civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Interregnum "Interrègne ottoman") lasted from 1402 to 1413 as Bayezid's sons fought over succession. It ended when [Mehmed I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmed_I "Mehmed I") emerged as the sultan and restored Ottoman power.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 363">: 363 </span></sup> 

The Balkan territories lost by the Ottomans after 1402, including Thessaloniki, Macedonia, and Kosovo, were later recovered by [Murad II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murad_II "Murad II") between the 1430s and 1450s. On 10 November 1444, Murad repelled the [Crusade of Varna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crusade_of_Varna "Croisade de Varna") by defeating the Hungarian, Polish, and [Wallachian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wallachia "Valachie") armies under [Władysław III of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_III_of_Poland "Ladislas III de Pologne") and [John Hunyadi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Hunyadi "Jean Hunyadi") at the [Battle of Varna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Varna "Bataille de Varna"), although Albanians under [Skanderbeg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skanderbeg "Skanderbeg") continued to resist. Four years later, John Hunyadi prepared another army of Hungarian and Wallachian forces to attack the Turks, but was again defeated at the [Second Battle of Kosovo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo_\(1448\) "Bataille du Kosovo (1448)") in 1448.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 29">: 29 </span></sup> 

According to modern historiography, there is a direct connection between the rapid Ottoman military advance and the consequences of the [Black Death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death "peste noire") from the mid-fourteenth century onwards. Byzantine territories, where the initial Ottoman conquests were carried out, were exhausted demographically and militarily due to the plague, which facilitated Ottoman expansion. In addition, slave hunting was the main economic driving force behind Ottoman conquest. Some 21st-century authors re-periodize conquest of the Balkans into the *akıncı phase*, which spanned 8 to 13 decades, characterized by continuous slave hunting and destruction, followed by administrative integration into the Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-Schmitt-Kiprovska_59-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Schmitt-Kiprovska-59"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nükhet_Varlik_60-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-N%C3%BCkhet_Varlik-60"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ayalon-2014_61-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Ayalon-2014-61"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Expansion and peak (1453–1566)

Main article: [Classical Age of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_Age_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "L'âge classique de l'Empire ottoman")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg/250px-Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg)

Sultan [Mehmed the Conqueror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmed_II "Mehmed II")'s entry into [Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantinople "Constantinople"); painting by [Fausto Zonaro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fausto_Zonaro "Fausto Zonaro") (1854–1929)

The son of Murad II, [Mehmed the Conqueror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmed_the_Conqueror "Mehmed le Conquérant"), reorganized both state and military, and on 29 May 1453 conquered [Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople "Chute de Constantinople"), ending the Byzantine Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-Quataert2005_63-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Quataert2005-63"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Mehmed allowed the [Eastern Orthodox Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church "Église orthodoxe orientale") to maintain its autonomy and land in exchange for accepting Ottoman authority.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_64-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-books.google-64"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Due to tension between the states of western Europe and the later Byzantine Empire, most of the Orthodox population accepted Ottoman rule, as preferable to Venetian rule.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_64-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-books.google-64"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Albanian resistance was a major obstacle to Ottoman expansion on the Italian peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

In the 15th and 16th centuries, the Ottoman Empire entered a [period of expansion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Growth_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Croissance de l'Empire ottoman"). The Empire prospered under the rule of a line of committed and effective [Sultans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Dynasty "Dynastie ottomane"). It flourished economically due to its control of the major overland trade routes between Europe and Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 111">: 111 </span></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>n<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

Sultan [Selim I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selim_I "Sélim Ier") (1512–1520) dramatically expanded the eastern and southern frontiers by defeating [Shah Ismail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ismail_I "Ismaïl Ier") of [Safavid Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_Iran "Iran safavide"), in the [Battle of Chaldiran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Chaldiran "Bataille de Chaldiran").<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / emplacement : 91–105">: 91–105 </span></sup>  Selim I established [Ottoman rule in Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt_Eyalet "Égypte Eyalet") by defeating and annexing the [Mamluk Sultanate of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate "Sultanat mamelouk") and created a naval presence on the [Red Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Sea "mer Rouge"). After this Ottoman expansion, competition began between the [Portuguese Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portuguese_Empire "Empire portugais") and the Ottomans to become the dominant power in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 55–76">: 55–76 </span></sup> 

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/EmperorSuleiman.jpg/250px-EmperorSuleiman.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:EmperorSuleiman.jpg)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Tizian_123.jpg/120px-Tizian_123.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tizian_123.jpg)

[Suleiman the Magnificent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent "Suleiman the Magnificent") and his wife [Hürrem Sultan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hurrem_Sultan "Hurrem Sultan"), by 16th century [Venetian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Venice "Republic of Venice") [painter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venetian_painting "Venetian painting") [Titian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titian "Titian")

[Suleiman the Magnificent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent "Suleiman the Magnificent") (1520–1566)<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> captured [Belgrade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belgrade "Belgrade") in 1521, conquered the southern and central parts of the [Kingdom of Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary "Kingdom of Hungary") as part of the [Ottoman–Hungarian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Hungarian_Wars "Ottoman–Hungarian Wars"), and, after his historic victory in the [Battle of Mohács](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs "Battle of Mohács") in 1526, he established Ottoman rule in the territory of present-day Hungary and other Central European territories. He then laid [siege to Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Vienna_\(1529\) "Siege of Vienna (1529)") in 1529, but failed to take the city.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 50">: 50 </span></sup>  In 1532, he made another [attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habsburg%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars_in_Hungary_\(1526%E2%80%931568\) "Habsburg–Ottoman wars in Hungary (1526–1568)") on Vienna, but was repulsed in the [siege of Güns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_G%C3%BCns "Siege of Güns").<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson442_72-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Thompson442-72"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ágoston_and_Alan_Masters583_73-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-%C3%81goston_and_Alan_Masters583-73"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Transylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transylvania "Transylvania"), Wallachia and, intermittently, [Moldavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moldavia "Moldavia"), became tributary principalities of the Empire. In the east, the Ottoman Turks [took](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Safavid_War_\(1532%E2%80%931555\) "Ottoman–Safavid War (1532–1555)") [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad") from the Persians in 1535, gaining control of [Mesopotamia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamia "Mesopotamia") and naval access to the [Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf "Persian Gulf"). In 1555, the [Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus "Caucasus") became partitioned for the first time between the Safavids and the Ottomans, a *[status quo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Status_quo "Status quo")* that remained until the end of the [Russo-Turkish War (1768–1774)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_\(1768%E2%80%931774\) "Russo-Turkish War (1768–1774)"). By this partitioning as signed in the [Peace of Amasya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peace_of_Amasya "Peace of Amasya"), [Western Armenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Armenia "Western Armenia"), western [Kurdistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdistan "Kurdistan"), and [Western Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Imereti "Kingdom of Imereti") fell into Ottoman hands,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> while southern [Dagestan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dagestan "Dagestan"), [Eastern Armenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Armenia "Eastern Armenia"), [Eastern Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Georgia_\(country\) "Eastern Georgia (country)"), and [Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan") remained Persian.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs%2C_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg/250px-Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs%2C_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg)

Ottoman miniature of the [Battle of Mohács](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs "Battle of Mohács") in 1526<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

In 1539, a 60,000-strong Ottoman army besieged the [Spanish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habsburg_Spain "Habsburg Spain") garrison of [Castelnuovo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Castelnuovo "Siege of Castelnuovo") on the [Adriatic coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adriatic_coast "Adriatic coast"); the successful siege cost the Ottomans 8,000 casualties,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> but [Venice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Venice "Republic of Venice") agreed to terms in 1540, surrendering most of its empire in the [Aegean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aegean_Sea "Aegean Sea") and the [Morea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morea "Morea"). [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_Modern_France "Early Modern France") and the Ottoman Empire, united by mutual opposition to [Habsburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habsburg "Habsburg") rule,<sup id="cite_ref-AksanOW_78-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-AksanOW-78"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> became allies. The French conquests of [Nice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Nice "Siege of Nice") (1543) and [Corsica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invasion_of_Corsica_\(1553\) "Invasion of Corsica (1553)") (1553) occurred as a joint venture between French king [Francis I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francis_I_of_France "Francis I of France") and Suleiman, and were commanded by the Ottoman admirals [Hayreddin Barbarossa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa "Hayreddin Barbarossa") and [Dragut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dragut "Dragut").<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> France supported the Ottomans with an artillery unit during the 1543 Ottoman [conquest of Esztergom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Esztergom_\(1543\) "Siege of Esztergom (1543)") in northern Hungary. After further advances by the Turks, the Habsburg ruler [Ferdinand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdinand_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor "Ferdinand I, Holy Roman Emperor") officially recognized Ottoman ascendancy in Hungary in 1547. Suleiman died of natural causes during the [siege of Szigetvár](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Szigetv%C3%A1r "Siege of Szigetvár") in 1566. Following his death, the Ottomans were said to be declining, although this has been rejected by many scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-decline_80-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-decline-80"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> By the end of Suleiman's reign, the Empire spanned approximately 877,888 sq mi (2,273,720 km<sup>2</sup>), extending over three continents.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 545">: 545 </span></sup> 

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/IAN_0137_Urrabieta_y_Ortiz_1859_Preveza.jpg/250px-IAN_0137_Urrabieta_y_Ortiz_1859_Preveza.jpg)

Ottoman admiral [Barbarossa Hayreddin Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa "Hayreddin Barbarossa") defeated the [Holy League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_League_\(1538\) "Holy League (1538)") of [Charles V](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor "Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor") under the command of [Andrea Doria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrea_Doria "Andrea Doria") at the [Battle of Preveza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Preveza "Battle of Preveza") in 1538.

The Empire became a dominant naval force, controlling much of the [Mediterranean Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea "Mediterranean Sea").<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 61">: 61 </span></sup>  The Empire was now a major part of European politics. The Ottomans became involved in multi-continental religious wars when Spain and Portugal were united under the [Iberian Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iberian_Union "Iberian Union"). The Ottomans were holders of the Caliph title, meaning they were the leaders of Muslims worldwide. The Iberians were leaders of the Christian crusaders, and so the two fought in a worldwide conflict. There were zones of operations in the Mediterranean<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and [Indian Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Ocean "Indian Ocean"),<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> where Iberians circumnavigated Africa to reach India and, on their way, wage war upon the Ottomans and their local Muslim allies. Likewise, the Iberians passed through newly-Christianized [Latin America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_America "Latin America") and [had sent expeditions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_de_Salcedo "Juan de Salcedo") that traversed the Pacific to Christianize the formerly Muslim Philippines and use it as a base to attack the Muslims in the [Far East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far_East "Far East").<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In this case, the Ottomans sent armies to aid its easternmost vassal and territory, the [Sultanate of Aceh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_Aceh "Sultanate of Aceh") in Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 84">: 84 </span></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

During the 1600s, the world conflict between the Ottoman Caliphate and Iberian Union was a stalemate since [both were at similar population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_in_1600 "List of countries by population in 1600"), technology and economic levels. Nevertheless, the success of the Ottoman political and military establishment was compared to the [Roman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire"), despite the difference in size, by the likes of contemporary Italian scholar [Francesco Sansovino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francesco_Sansovino "Francesco Sansovino") and French political philosopher [Jean Bodin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Bodin "Jean Bodin").<sup id="cite_ref-deringil709_88-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-deringil709-88"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Stagnation and reform (1566–1827)

#### Revolts, reversals, and revivals (1566–1683)

Main article: [Transformation of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transformation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Transformation of the Ottoman Empire")

Further information: [Ottoman decline thesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_decline_thesis "Ottoman decline thesis")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/IstanbulNavalMuseum38.JPG/250px-IstanbulNavalMuseum38.JPG)

Late 16th or early 17th century [Ottoman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Navy "Ottoman Navy") [galley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galley "Galley") known as *[Tarihi Kadırga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tarihi_Kad%C4%B1rga "Tarihi Kadırga")* at the [Istanbul Naval Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul_Naval_Museum "Istanbul Naval Museum"), built in the period between the reigns of Sultan [Murad III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murad_III "Murad III") (1574–1595) and Sultan [Mehmed IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmed_IV "Mehmed IV") (1648–1687)<sup id="cite_ref-kadirga1_89-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-kadirga1-89"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kadirga2_90-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-kadirga2-90"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

In the second half of the sixteenth century, the Ottoman Empire came under increasing strain from inflation and the rapidly rising costs of warfare that were impacting both Europe and the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> These pressures led to a series of crises around the year 1600, placing great strain upon the Ottoman system of government.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 413–414">: 413–414 </span></sup>  The empire underwent a series of transformations of its political and military institutions in response to these challenges, enabling it to successfully adapt to the new conditions of the seventeenth century and remain powerful, both militarily and economically.<sup id="cite_ref-decline_80-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-decline-80"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 10">: 10 </span></sup>  Historians of the mid-twentieth century once characterised this period as one of stagnation and decline, but this view is now rejected by the majority of academics.<sup id="cite_ref-decline_80-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-decline-80"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The discovery of new maritime trade routes by Western European states allowed them to avoid the Ottoman trade monopoly. The [Portuguese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal "Kingdom of Portugal") discovery of the [Cape of Good Hope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope "Cape of Good Hope") in 1488 initiated [a series of Ottoman-Portuguese naval wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_naval_expeditions_in_the_Indian_Ocean "Ottoman naval expeditions in the Indian Ocean") in the [Indian Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Ocean "Indian Ocean") throughout the 16th century. Despite the growing European presence in the Indian Ocean, Ottoman trade with the east continued to flourish. Cairo, in particular, benefitted from the rise of Yemeni coffee as a popular consumer commodity. As coffeehouses appeared in cities and towns across the empire, Cairo developed into a major center for its trade, contributing to its continued prosperity throughout the seventeenth and much of the eighteenth century.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 507–508">: 507–508 </span></sup> 

Under [Ivan IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivan_IV "Ivan IV") (1533–1584), the [Tsardom of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia "Tsardom of Russia") expanded into the Volga and Caspian regions at the expense of the Tatar khanates. In 1571, the Crimean khan [Devlet I Giray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Devlet_I_Giray "Devlet I Giray"), commanded by the Ottomans, [burned Moscow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fire_of_Moscow_\(1571\) "Fire of Moscow (1571)").<sup id="cite_ref-Davies2007_95-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Davies2007-95"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The next year, the invasion was repeated but repelled at the [Battle of Molodi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Molodi "Battle of Molodi"). The Ottoman Empire continued to invade Eastern Europe in a series of [slave raids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_conflicts_in_Europe_during_Turco-Mongol_rule "List of conflicts in Europe during Turco-Mongol rule"),<sup id="cite_ref-Subtelny2000_96-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Subtelny2000-96"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and remained a significant power in Eastern Europe until the end of the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Giorgio-vasari-battle-of-lepanto.jpg/250px-Giorgio-vasari-battle-of-lepanto.jpg)

Order of battle of the two fleets in the [Battle of Lepanto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto "Battle of Lepanto"), with an allegory of the three powers of the [Holy League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_League_\(1571\) "Holy League (1571)") in the foreground, fresco by [Giorgio Vasari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giorgio_Vasari "Giorgio Vasari")

The Ottomans decided to conquer [Venetian Cyprus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venetian_Cyprus "Venetian Cyprus") and on 22 July 1570, Nicosia was besieged; 50,000 Christians died, and 180,000 were enslaved.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 67">: 67 </span></sup>  On 15 September 1570, the Ottoman cavalry appeared before the last Venetian stronghold in Cyprus, Famagusta. The Venetian defenders held out for 11 months against a force that at its peak numbered 200,000 men with 145 cannons; 163,000 cannonballs struck the walls of Famagusta before it fell to the Ottomans in August 1571. The [Siege of Famagusta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Famagusta "Siege of Famagusta") claimed 50,000 Ottoman casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 328">: 328 </span></sup>  Meanwhile, the [Holy League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_League_\(1571\) "Holy League (1571)") consisting of mostly Spanish and Venetian fleets won a victory over the Ottoman fleet at the [Battle of Lepanto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto "Battle of Lepanto") (1571), off southwestern Greece; Catholic forces killed over 30,000 Turks and destroyed 200 of their ships.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 24">: 24 </span></sup>  It was a startling, if mostly symbolic,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979272_101-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979272-101"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> blow to the image of Ottoman invincibility, an image which the victory of the Knights of Malta over the Ottoman invaders in the 1565 [siege of Malta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Siege_of_Malta "Great Siege of Malta") had recently set about eroding.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The battle was far more damaging to the Ottoman navy in sapping experienced manpower than the loss of ships, which were rapidly replaced.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 53">: 53 </span></sup>  The Ottoman navy recovered quickly, persuading Venice to sign a peace treaty in 1573, allowing the Ottomans to expand and consolidate their position in North Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198067_104-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198067-104"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

By contrast, the Habsburg frontier had settled somewhat, a stalemate caused by a stiffening of the Habsburg defenses.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198071_105-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198071-105"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Long Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_Turkish_War "Long Turkish War") against Habsburg Austria (1593–1606) created the need for greater numbers of Ottoman infantry equipped with firearms, resulting in a relaxation of recruitment policy. This contributed to problems of indiscipline and outright rebelliousness within the corps, which were never fully solved.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198090–92_106-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198090%E2%80%9392-106"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:AGE_MATTERS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:AGE MATTERS"><span title="This claim needs references to more current sources. (September 2016)">obsolete&nbsp;source</span></a></i>]</sup> Irregular sharpshooters ([Sekban](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sekban "Sekban")) were also recruited, and on demobilisation turned to [brigandage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brigandage "Brigandage") in the [Celali rebellions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celali_rebellions "Celali rebellions") (1590–1610), which engendered widespread anarchy in [Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolia "Anatolia") in the late 16th and early 17th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 24">: 24 </span></sup>  With the Empire's population reaching 30 million people by 1600, the shortage of land placed further pressure on the government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979281_108-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979281-108"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:AGE_MATTERS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:AGE MATTERS"><span title="This claim needs references to more current sources. (September 2016)">obsolete&nbsp;source</span></a></i>]</sup> In spite of these problems, the Ottoman state remained strong, and its army did not collapse or suffer crushing defeats. The only exceptions were campaigns against the [Safavid dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_dynasty "Safavid dynasty") of Persia, where many of the Ottoman eastern provinces were lost, some permanently. This [1603–1618 war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Safavid_War_\(1603%E2%80%931618\) "Ottoman–Safavid War (1603–1618)") eventually resulted in the [Treaty of Nasuh Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Nasuh_Pasha "Treaty of Nasuh Pasha"), which ceded the entire Caucasus, except westernmost Georgia, back into the possession of [Safavid Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_Iran "Safavid Iran").<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The treaty ending the [Cretan War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cretan_War_\(1645%E2%80%931669\) "Cretan War (1645–1669)") cost Venice much of [Dalmatia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venetian_Dalmatia "Venetian Dalmatia"), its Aegean island possessions, and [Crete](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Candia "Kingdom of Candia"). (Losses from the war totalled 30,985 Venetian soldiers and 118,754 Turkish soldiers.)<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 33">: 33 </span></sup> 

During his brief majority reign, [Murad IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murad_IV "Murad IV") (1623–1640) reasserted central authority and recaptured [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq") (1639) from the Safavids.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198073_111-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198073-111"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The resulting [Treaty of Zuhab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Zuhab "Treaty of Zuhab") of that same year decisively divided the Caucasus and adjacent regions between the two neighbouring empires as it had already been defined in the 1555 Peace of Amasya.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The [Sultanate of Women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_Women "Sultanate of Women") (1533–1656) was a period in which the mothers of young sultans exercised power on behalf of their sons. The most prominent women of this period were [Kösem Sultan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C3%B6sem_Sultan "Kösem Sultan") and her daughter-in-law [Turhan Hatice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turhan_Hatice "Turhan Hatice"), whose political rivalry culminated in Kösem's murder in 1651.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198074–75_114-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198074%E2%80%9375-114"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> During the [Köprülü era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C3%B6pr%C3%BCl%C3%BC_era "Köprülü era") (1656–1703), effective control of the Empire was exercised by a sequence of [grand viziers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_vizier "Grand vizier") from the Köprülü family. The Köprülü Vizierate saw renewed military success with authority restored in Transylvania, the conquest of [Crete](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crete "Crete") completed in 1669, and expansion into [Polish southern Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Ukraine#Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth "History of Ukraine"), with the strongholds of [Khotyn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khotyn "Khotyn"), and [Kamianets-Podilskyi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamianets-Podilskyi "Kamianets-Podilskyi") and the territory of [Podolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Podolia "Podolia") ceding to Ottoman control in 1676.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198080–81_115-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198080%E2%80%9381-115"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg/250px-Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg)

The [Second Siege of Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna "Battle of Vienna") in 1683, by [Frans Geffels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frans_Geffels "Frans Geffels") (1624–1694)

This period of renewed assertiveness came to a calamitous end in 1683 when Grand Vizier [Kara Mustafa Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kara_Mustafa_Pasha "Kara Mustafa Pasha") led a huge army to attempt a second Ottoman siege of [Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Vienna "History of Vienna") in the [Great Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Turkish_War "Great Turkish War") of 1683–1699. The final assault being fatally delayed, the Ottoman forces were swept away by allied Habsburg, German, and Polish forces spearheaded by the Polish king [John III Sobieski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_III_Sobieski "John III Sobieski") at the [Battle of Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna "Battle of Vienna"). The alliance of the [Holy League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_League_\(1684\) "Holy League (1684)") pressed home the advantage of the defeat at Vienna, culminating in the [Treaty of Karlowitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Karlowitz "Treaty of Karlowitz") (26 January 1699), which ended the Great Turkish War.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979357_116-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979357-116"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Ottomans surrendered control of significant territories, many permanently.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198084_117-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198084-117"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Mustafa II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_II "Mustafa II") (1695–1703) led the counterattack of 1695–1696 against the Habsburgs in Hungary, but was undone at the disastrous defeat at [Zenta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Zenta "Battle of Zenta") (in modern Serbia), 11 September 1697.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198083–84_118-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198083%E2%80%9384-118"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

#### Military defeats

Aside from the loss of the [Banat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banat "Banat") and the temporary loss of [Belgrade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Belgrade "History of Belgrade") (1717–1739), the Ottoman border on the [Danube](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danube "Danube") and [Sava](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sava "Sava") remained stable during the eighteenth century. [Russian expansion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expansion_of_Russia_1500%E2%80%931800 "Expansion of Russia 1500–1800"), however, presented a large and growing threat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371_119-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371-119"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Accordingly, King [Charles XII of Sweden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_XII_of_Sweden "Charles XII of Sweden") was welcomed as an ally in the Ottoman Empire following his defeat by the Russians at the [Battle of Poltava](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Poltava "Battle of Poltava") of 1709 in central Ukraine (part of the [Great Northern War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Northern_War "Great Northern War") of 1700–1721).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371_119-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371-119"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Charles XII persuaded the Ottoman Sultan [Ahmed III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmed_III "Ahmed III") to declare war on Russia, which resulted in an Ottoman victory in the [Pruth River Campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pruth_River_Campaign "Pruth River Campaign") of 1710–1711, in Moldavia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979372_120-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979372-120"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG/250px-1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG)

Austrian troops led by [Prince Eugene of Savoy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_Eugene_of_Savoy "Prince Eugene of Savoy") capture [Belgrade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belgrade "Belgrade") in 1717. Austrian control in Serbia lasted until the Turkish victory in the [Austro-Russian–Turkish War (1735–1739)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_\(1735%E2%80%931739\) "Russo-Turkish War (1735–1739)"). With the 1739 [Treaty of Belgrade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Belgrade "Treaty of Belgrade"), the Ottoman Empire regained northern [Bosnia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina "Bosnia and Herzegovina"), [Habsburg Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_\(1718%E2%80%931739\) "Kingdom of Serbia (1718–1739)") (including Belgrade), [Oltenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oltenia "Oltenia") and the southern parts of the [Banat of Temeswar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banat_of_Temeswar "Banat of Temeswar").

After the [Austro-Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austro-Turkish_War_\(1716%E2%80%931718\) "Austro-Turkish War (1716–1718)"), the [Treaty of Passarowitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Passarowitz "Treaty of Passarowitz") confirmed the loss of the Banat, Serbia, and ["Little Walachia" (Oltenia)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oltenia "Oltenia") to Austria. The Treaty also revealed that the Ottoman Empire was on the defensive and unlikely to present any further aggression in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979376_121-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979376-121"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Austro-Russian–Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austro-Russian%E2%80%93Turkish_War_\(1735%E2%80%931739\) "Austro-Russian–Turkish War (1735–1739)") (1735–1739), which was ended by the [Treaty of Belgrade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Belgrade "Treaty of Belgrade") in 1739, resulted in the Ottoman recovery of northern [Bosnia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnia "Bosnia"), [Habsburg Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_\(1718%E2%80%931739\) "Kingdom of Serbia (1718–1739)") (including Belgrade), [Oltenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oltenia "Oltenia") and the southern parts of the [Banat of Temeswar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banat_of_Temeswar "Banat of Temeswar"); but the Empire lost the port of [Azov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azov "Azov"), north of the Crimean Peninsula, to the Russians. After this treaty the Ottoman Empire was able to enjoy a generation of peace in Europe, as Austria and Russia were forced to deal with the rise of [Prussia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prussia "Prussia").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979392_122-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979392-122"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

[Educational and technological reforms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_and_Technology_in_the_Ottoman_Empire#Education "Science and Technology in the Ottoman Empire") came about, including the establishment of higher education institutions such as the [Istanbul Technical University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul_Technical_University "Istanbul Technical University").<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 1734 an artillery school was established to impart Western-style artillery methods, but the Islamic clergy successfully objected under the grounds of [theodicy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodicy "Theodicy").<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_a_124-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-books.google_a-124"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 1754 the artillery school was reopened on a semi-secret basis.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_a_124-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-books.google_a-124"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 1726, [Ibrahim Muteferrika](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibrahim_Muteferrika "Ibrahim Muteferrika") convinced the Grand Vizier [Nevşehirli Damat Ibrahim Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nev%C5%9Fehirli_Damat_Ibrahim_Pasha "Nevşehirli Damat Ibrahim Pasha"), the [Grand Mufti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Mufti "Grand Mufti"), and the clergy on the efficiency of the printing press, and Muteferrika was later granted by Sultan Ahmed III permission to publish non-religious books (despite opposition from some [calligraphers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calligraphy "Islamic calligraphy") and religious leaders).<sup id="cite_ref-katip_celebi_125-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-katip_celebi-125"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Muteferrika's press published its first book in 1729 and, by 1743, issued 17 works in 23 volumes, each having between 500 and 1,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-katip_celebi_125-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-katip_celebi-125"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-watson_126-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-watson-126"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

In North Africa, Spain [conquered Oran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Oran_\(1732\) "Spanish conquest of Oran (1732)") from the autonomous [Deylik of Algiers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deylik_of_Algiers "Deylik of Algiers"). The [Bey of Oran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beylik_of_Oran "Beylik of Oran") received an army from Algiers, but it failed to recapture [Oran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oran "Oran"); the siege caused the deaths of 1,500 Spaniards, and even more Algerians. The Spanish also massacred many Muslim soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 1792, Spain abandoned Oran, selling it to the Deylik of Algiers.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg/220px-January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg)

Ottoman troops attempting to halt the advancing Russians during the [Siege of Ochakov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Ochakov_\(1788\) "Siege of Ochakov (1788)") in 1788

In 1768 Russian-backed Ukrainian [Haidamakas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haidamaka "Haidamaka"), pursuing Polish confederates, entered [Balta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balta,_Ukraine "Balta, Ukraine"), an Ottoman-controlled town on the border of Bessarabia in Ukraine, massacred its citizens, and burned the town to the ground. This action provoked the Ottoman Empire into the [Russo-Turkish War of 1768–1774](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_\(1768%E2%80%931774\) "Russo-Turkish War (1768–1774)"). The [Treaty of Küçük Kaynarca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_Kaynarca "Treaty of Küçük Kaynarca") of 1774 ended the war and provided freedom of worship for the Christian citizens of the Ottoman-controlled provinces of Wallachia and Moldavia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979405_128-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979405-128"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> By the late 18th century, after a number of defeats in the wars with Russia, some people in the Ottoman Empire began to conclude that the reforms of [Peter the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_the_Great "Peter the Great") had given the Russians an edge, and the Ottomans would have to keep up with Western technology in order to avoid further defeats.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_a_124-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-books.google_a-124"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg/250px-Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg)

[Selim III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selim_III "Selim III") receiving dignitaries during an audience at the Gate of Felicity, [Topkapı Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace "Topkapı Palace"). Painting by [Konstantin Kapıdağlı](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Konstantin_Kap%C4%B1da%C4%9Fl%C4%B1 "Konstantin Kapıdağlı")

[Selim III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selim_III "Selim III") (1789–1807) made the first major attempts to [modernise the army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_military_reform_efforts "Ottoman military reform efforts"), but his reforms were hampered by the religious leadership and the [Janissary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Janissary "Janissary") corps. Jealous of their privileges and firmly opposed to change, the Janissary [revolted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Janissary_revolts "Janissary revolts"). Selim's efforts cost him his throne and his life, but were resolved in spectacular and bloody fashion by his successor, the dynamic [Mahmud II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_II "Mahmud II"), who [eliminated the Janissary corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auspicious_Incident "Auspicious Incident") in 1826.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Gen%C3%A8ve_et_Gr%C3%A8ce_-_Bataille_de_l%27Acropole_par_JGC_Perlberg.jpg/250px-Gen%C3%A8ve_et_Gr%C3%A8ce_-_Bataille_de_l%27Acropole_par_JGC_Perlberg.jpg)

The siege of the Acropolis in 1826–1827 during the [Greek War of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence "Greek War of Independence")

The [Serbian revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbian_revolution "Serbian revolution") (1804–1815) marked the beginning of an era of [national awakening](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rise_of_nationalism_under_the_Ottoman_Empire "Rise of nationalism under the Ottoman Empire") in the [Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkans "Balkans") during the [Eastern Question](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Question "Eastern Question"). In 1811, the fundamentalist Wahhabis of Arabia, led by the al-Saud family, revolted against the Ottomans. Unable to defeat the Wahhabi rebels, the Sublime Porte had [Muhammad Ali Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt "Muhammad Ali of Egypt") of [Kavala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kavala "Kavala"), the *[vali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wali "Wali")* (governor) of the [Eyalet of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt_Eyalet "Egypt Eyalet"), tasked with retaking Arabia, which ended with the destruction of the [Emirate of Diriyah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Diriyah "Emirate of Diriyah") in 1818. The [suzerainty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suzerainty "Suzerainty") of Serbia as a hereditary monarchy under its own [dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obrenovi%C4%87_dynasty "Obrenović dynasty") was acknowledged *[de jure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_jure "De jure")* in 1830.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Berend2003_130-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Berend2003-130"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 1821, the [Greeks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Greece "Ottoman Greece") [declared war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence "Greek War of Independence") on the Sultan.
