A rebellion that originated in Moldavia as a diversion was followed by the main revolution in the [Peloponnese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peloponnese "Peloponnese"), which, along with the northern part of the [Gulf of Corinth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Corinth "Gulf of Corinth"), became the first parts of the Ottoman Empire to achieve independence (in 1829). In 1830, the French invaded the [Deylik of Algiers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deylik_of_Algiers "Deylik of Algiers"). [The campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invasion_of_Algiers_in_1830 "Invasion of Algiers in 1830") that took 21 days, resulted in over 5,000 Algerian military casualties,<sup id="cite_ref-De_Quatrebarbes-1831_131-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-De_Quatrebarbes-1831-131"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and about 2,600 French ones.<sup id="cite_ref-De_Quatrebarbes-1831_131-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-De_Quatrebarbes-1831-131"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Before the French invasion the total population of Algeria was most likely between 3,000,000 and 5,000,000.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> By 1873, the population of Algeria (excluding several hundred thousand newly arrived French settlers) had decreased to 2,172,000.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 1831, [Muhammad Ali of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt "Muhammad Ali of Egypt") revolted against Sultan [Mahmud II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_II "Mahmud II") due to the latter's refusal to grant him the governorships of [Greater Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria_\(region\) "Syria (region)") and [Crete](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crete "Crete"), which the Sultan had promised him in exchange for sending military assistance to put down the [Greek revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence "Greek War of Independence") (1821–1829) that ultimately ended with the formal [independence of Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_Protocol_\(1830\) "London Protocol (1830)") in 1830. It was a costly enterprise for Muhammad Ali, who had lost his fleet at the [Battle of Navarino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Navarino "Battle of Navarino") in 1827. Thus began the first [Egyptian–Ottoman War (1831–1833)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian%E2%80%93Ottoman_War_\(1831%E2%80%931833\) "Egyptian–Ottoman War (1831–1833)"), during which the French-trained army of Muhammad Ali, under the command of his son [Ibrahim Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibrahim_Pasha_of_Egypt "Ibrahim Pasha of Egypt"), defeated the Ottoman Army as it marched into [Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolia "Anatolia"), reaching the city of [Kütahya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C3%BCtahya "Kütahya") within 320 km (200 mi) of the capital, Constantinople.<sup id="cite_ref-Effraim_135-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Effraim-135"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 95">: 95 </span></sup>  In desperation, Sultan [Mahmud II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_II "Mahmud II") appealed to the empire's traditional arch-rival Russia for help, asking Emperor [Nicholas I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Russia "Nicholas I of Russia") to send an expeditionary force to assist him.<sup id="cite_ref-Effraim_135-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Effraim-135"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 96">: 96 </span></sup>  In return for signing the [Treaty of Hünkâr İskelesi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_H%C3%BCnk%C3%A2r_%C4%B0skelesi "Treaty of Hünkâr İskelesi"), the Russians sent the expeditionary force which deterred Ibrahim Pasha from marching any further towards Constantinople.<sup id="cite_ref-Effraim_135-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Effraim-135"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 96">: 96 </span></sup>  Under the terms of the [Convention of Kütahya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convention_of_K%C3%BCtahya "Convention of Kütahya"), signed on 5 May 1833, Muhammad Ali agreed to abandon his campaign against the Sultan, in exchange for which he was made the *[vali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wali "Wali")* (governor) of the *[vilayets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vilayet "Vilayet")* (provinces) of [Crete](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crete "Crete"), [Aleppo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleppo "Aleppo"), [Tripoli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tripoli,_Lebanon "Tripoli, Lebanon"), [Damascus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Damascus "Damascus") and [Sidon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidon "Sidon") (the latter four comprising modern [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria "Syria") and [Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanon "Lebanon")), and given the right to collect taxes in [Adana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adana "Adana").<sup id="cite_ref-Effraim_135-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Effraim-135"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 96">: 96 </span></sup>  Had it not been for the Russian intervention, Sultan [Mahmud II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_II "Mahmud II") could have faced the risk of being overthrown and Muhammad Ali could have even become the new Sultan. These events marked the beginning of a recurring pattern where the Sublime Porte needed the help of foreign powers to protect itself.<sup id="cite_ref-Effraim_135-4" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Effraim-135"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 95–96">: 95–96 </span></sup> 

In 1839, the [Sublime Porte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sublime_Porte "Sublime Porte") attempted to take back what it lost to the *[de facto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_facto "De facto")* autonomous, but *[de jure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_jure "De jure")* still Ottoman [Eyalet of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt_Eyalet "Egypt Eyalet"), but its forces were initially defeated, which led to the [Oriental Crisis of 1840](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oriental_Crisis_of_1840 "Oriental Crisis of 1840"). Muhammad Ali had close relations with [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/July_Monarchy "July Monarchy"), and the prospect of him becoming the Sultan of Egypt was widely viewed as putting the entire [Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levant "Levant") into the French sphere of influence.<sup id="cite_ref-Effraim_135-5" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Effraim-135"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 96">: 96 </span></sup>  As the Sublime Porte had proved itself incapable of defeating Muhammad Ali,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> the [British Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") and [Austrian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrian_Empire "Austrian Empire") provided military assistance, and the second [Egyptian–Ottoman War (1839–1841)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian%E2%80%93Ottoman_War_\(1839%E2%80%931841\) "Egyptian–Ottoman War (1839–1841)") ended with Ottoman victory and the restoration of Ottoman suzerainty over [Egypt Eyalet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt_Eyalet "Egypt Eyalet") and the [Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levant "Levant").<sup id="cite_ref-Effraim_135-6" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Effraim-135"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 96">: 96 </span></sup> 

By the mid-19th century, the Ottoman Empire was called the "[sick man of Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sick_man_of_Europe "Sick man of Europe")". Three suzerain states – the [Principality of Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia "Principality of Serbia"), [Wallachia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wallachia "Wallachia") and [Moldavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moldavia "Moldavia") – moved towards *de jure* independence during the 1860s and 1870s.

### Decline and modernisation (1828–1908)

Main article: [Decline of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decline_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Decline of the Ottoman Empire")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Opening_ceremony_of_the_First_Ottoman_Parliament_at_the_Dolmabahce_Palace_in_1876.jpg/250px-Opening_ceremony_of_the_First_Ottoman_Parliament_at_the_Dolmabahce_Palace_in_1876.jpg)

Opening ceremony of the First [Ottoman Parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "General Assembly of the Ottoman Empire") at the [Dolmabahçe Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace "Dolmabahçe Palace") in 1876. The [First Constitutional Era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Constitutional_Era "First Constitutional Era") lasted only two years until 1878. The Ottoman Constitution and Parliament were [restored 30 years later](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era "Second Constitutional Era") with the [Young Turk Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution "Young Turk Revolution") in 1908.

During the [Tanzimat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanzimat "Tanzimat") period (1839–1876), the government's series of constitutional reforms led to a fairly modern [conscripted army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscription_in_the_Ottoman_Empire "Conscription in the Ottoman Empire"), banking system reforms, the decriminalization of homosexuality, the replacement of religious law with secular law,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and guilds with modern factories. The Ottoman Ministry of Post was established in Istanbul in 1840. American inventor [Samuel Morse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_Morse "Samuel Morse") received an Ottoman patent for the telegraph in 1847, issued by Sultan [Abdülmecid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abd%C3%BClmecid_I "Abdülmecid I"), who personally tested the invention.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The reformist period peaked with the Constitution, called the *[Kanûn-u Esâsî](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kan%C3%BBn-u_Es%C3%A2s%C3%AE "Kanûn-u Esâsî")*. The empire's [First Constitutional era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Constitutional_Era_\(Ottoman_Empire\) "First Constitutional Era (Ottoman Empire)") was short-lived. The parliament survived for only two years before the sultan suspended it.

The empire's Christian population, owing to their higher educational levels, started to pull ahead of the Muslim majority, leading to much resentment.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_b_140-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-books.google_b-140"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 1861, there were 571 primary and 94 secondary schools for Ottoman Christians, with 140,000 pupils in total, a figure that vastly exceeded the number of Muslim children in school at the time, who were further hindered by the amount of time spent learning Arabic and Islamic theology.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_b_140-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-books.google_b-140"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Author Norman Stone suggests that the Arabic alphabet, in which Turkish was written [until 1928](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_alphabet_reform "Turkish alphabet reform"), was ill-suited to reflect the sounds of Turkish (which is a Turkic as opposed to Semitic language), which imposed further difficulty on Turkish children.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_b_140-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-books.google_b-140"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In turn, Christians' higher educational levels allowed them to play a larger role in the economy, with the rise in prominence of groups such as the [Sursock family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sursock_family "Sursock family") indicative of this.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-books.google_b_140-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-books.google_b-140"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 1911, of the 654 wholesale companies in Istanbul, 528 were owned by ethnic Greeks.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_b_140-4" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-books.google_b-140"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In many cases, Christians and Jews gained protection from European consuls and citizenship, meaning they were protected from Ottoman law and not subject to the same economic regulations as their Muslim counterparts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERogan201193_142-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTERogan201193-142"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Turkish_troops_storming_Fort_Shefketil_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Turkish_troops_storming_Fort_Shefketil_%28cropped%29.jpg)

Ottoman troops storming [Fort Shefketil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shekvetili "Shekvetili") during the [Crimean War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_War "Crimean War") of 1853–1856

The [Crimean War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_War "Crimean War") (1853–1856) was part of a long-running contest between the major European powers for influence over territories of the declining Ottoman Empire. The financial burden of the war led the Ottoman state to issue [foreign loans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_public_debt "Ottoman public debt") amounting to 5 million pounds sterling on 4 August 1854.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 32">: 32 </span></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 71">: 71 </span></sup>  The war caused an exodus of the [Crimean Tatars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_Tatars "Crimean Tatars"), about 200,000 of whom moved to the Ottoman Empire in continuing waves of emigration.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 79–108">: 79–108 </span></sup>  Toward the end of the [Caucasian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasian_Wars "Caucasian Wars"), 90% of the [Circassians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circassians "Circassians") were [ethnically cleansed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_of_Circassians "Ethnic cleansing of Circassians")<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and exiled from their homelands in the Caucasus, fleeing to the Ottoman Empire,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> resulting in the settlement of 500,000 to 700,000 Circassians in the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamed-Troyansky202449_148-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamed-Troyansky202449-148"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Crimean Tatar refugees in the late 19th century played an especially notable role in seeking to modernise Ottoman education and in first promoting both [Pan-Turkism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan-Turkism "Pan-Turkism") and a sense of Turkish nationalism.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_149-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-ReferenceA-149"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Charles_Porion_-_The_kings_of_Europe_in_Paris_for_the_opening_of_the_Exposition_of_1867.jpg/330px-Charles_Porion_-_The_kings_of_Europe_in_Paris_for_the_opening_of_the_Exposition_of_1867.jpg)

The Kings of Europe are in [Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris "Paris") ([Napoleon III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleon_III "Napoleon III") is at the centre, Sultan [Abdulaziz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdulaziz "Abdulaziz") is second from right) for the opening of the [Universal Exposition of 1867](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exposition_Universelle_\(1867\) "Exposition Universelle (1867)")

In this period, the Ottoman Empire spent only small amounts of public funds on education; for example, in 1860–1861 only 0.2% of the total budget was invested in education.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 50">: 50 </span></sup>  As the Ottoman state attempted to modernize its infrastructure and army in response to outside threats, it opened itself up to a different kind of threat: that of creditors. As the historian Eugene Rogan has written, "the single greatest threat to the independence of the Middle East" in the 19th century "was not the armies of Europe but its banks".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERogan2011105_151-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTERogan2011105-151"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Ottoman state, which had begun taking on debt with the Crimean War, was forced to declare bankruptcy in 1875.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERogan2011106_152-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTERogan2011106-152"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> By 1881, the Ottoman Empire agreed to have its debt controlled by the [Ottoman Public Debt Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Public_Debt_Administration "Ottoman Public Debt Administration"), a council of European men with presidency alternating between France and Britain. The body controlled swaths of the Ottoman economy, and used its position to ensure that European capital continued to penetrate the empire, often to the detriment of local Ottoman interests.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERogan2011106_152-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTERogan2011106-152"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Ottomans_1875.png/250px-Ottomans_1875.png)

The Ottoman Empire in 1875 under Sultan [Abdulaziz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdulaziz "Abdulaziz")

The Ottoman [bashi-bazouks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bashi-bazouk "Bashi-bazouk") suppressed the [Bulgarian uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/April_Uprising "April Uprising") of 1876, massacring up to 100,000 people in the process.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 139">: 139 </span></sup>  The [Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_\(1877%E2%80%931878\) "Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)") ended with a decisive victory for Russia. As a result, Ottoman holdings in Europe declined sharply: [Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principality_of_Bulgaria "Principality of Bulgaria") was established as an independent principality inside the Ottoman Empire; [Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Principalities "United Principalities") achieved full independence; and [Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Serbia "History of Serbia") and [Montenegro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montenegro "Montenegro") finally gained complete independence, but with smaller territories. In 1878, [Austria-Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria-Hungary "Austria-Hungary") unilaterally occupied the Ottoman provinces of [Bosnia-Herzegovina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnia_Vilayet "Bosnia Vilayet") and [Novi Pazar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanjak_of_Novi_Pazar "Sanjak of Novi Pazar").

British Prime Minister [Benjamin Disraeli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli "Benjamin Disraeli") advocated restoring the Ottoman territories on the Balkan Peninsula during the [Congress of Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin "Congress of Berlin"), and in return, Britain assumed the administration of [Cyprus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus "Cyprus") in 1878.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 228–254">: 228–254 </span></sup>  Britain later sent troops to [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt") in 1882 to put down the [Urabi Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urabi_Revolt "Urabi Revolt") (Sultan [Abdul Hamid II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdul_Hamid_II "Abdul Hamid II") was too paranoid to mobilize his own army, fearing this would result in a coup d'état), effectively gaining control in both territories. Abdul Hamid II was so fearful of a coup that he did not allow his army to conduct war games, lest this serve as cover for a coup, but he did see the need for military mobilization. In 1883, a German military mission under General Baron [Colmar von der Goltz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colmar_Freiherr_von_der_Goltz "Colmar Freiherr von der Goltz") arrived to train the Ottoman Army, leading to the so-called "Goltz generation" of German-trained officers, who played a notable role in the politics of the empire's last years.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 24">: 24 </span></sup> 

From 1894 to 1896, between 100,000 and 300,000 Armenians living throughout the empire were killed in what became known as the [Hamidian massacres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamidian_massacres "Hamidian massacres").<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-156"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 42">: 42 </span></sup> 

In 1897 the population was 19 million, of whom 14 million (74%) were Muslim. An additional 20 million lived in provinces that remained under the sultan's nominal suzerainty but were entirely outside his actual power. One by one the Porte lost nominal authority. They included Egypt, Tunisia, Bulgaria, Cyprus, Bosnia-Herzegovina, and Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

As the Ottoman Empire gradually shrank, 7–9 million Muslims from its former territories in the Caucasus, [Crimea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimea "Crimea"), Balkans, and the [Mediterranean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean "Mediterranean") islands migrated to Anatolia and [Eastern Thrace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Thrace "Eastern Thrace").<sup id="cite_ref-Karpat2004_158-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Karpat2004-158"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> After the Empire lost the [First Balkan War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Balkan_War "First Balkan War") (1912–1913), it lost all its [Balkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkan_peninsula "Balkan peninsula") territories except [East Thrace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Thrace "East Thrace") (European Turkey). This resulted in around 400,000 Muslims fleeing with the retreating Ottoman armies (with many dying from [cholera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cholera "Cholera") brought by the soldiers), and 400,000 non-Muslims fled territory still under Ottoman rule.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Justin McCarthy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justin_McCarthy_\(American_historian\) "Justin McCarthy (American historian)") estimates that from 1821 to 1922, 5.5 million Muslims died in southeastern Europe, with the expulsion of 5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-McCarthy1995_163-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-McCarthy1995-163"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carmichael2012_164-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Carmichael2012-164"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Buturovic2010_165-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Buturovic2010-165"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Defeat and dissolution (1908–1922)

Main articles: [Dissolution of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Dissolution of the Ottoman Empire") and [Ottoman Empire in World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire_in_World_War_I "Ottoman Empire in World War I")

#### Young Turk movement

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png/250px-Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png)

Declaration of the [Young Turk Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution "Young Turk Revolution") by the leaders of the Ottoman [millets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Millet_\(Ottoman_Empire\) "Millet (Ottoman Empire)") in 1908

The defeat and [dissolution of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Dissolution of the Ottoman Empire") (1908—1922) began with the [Second Constitutional Era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era "Second Constitutional Era"), a moment of hope and promise established with the [Young Turk Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution "Young Turk Revolution"). It restored the [Constitution of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Constitution of the Ottoman Empire") and brought in [multi-party politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_Ottoman_Empire "List of political parties in the Ottoman Empire") with a [two-stage electoral system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elections_in_the_Ottoman_Empire "Elections in the Ottoman Empire") ([electoral law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_electoral_law "Ottoman electoral law")) under the [Ottoman parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "General Assembly of the Ottoman Empire"). The constitution offered hope by freeing the empire's citizens to modernise the state's institutions, rejuvenate its strength, and enable it to hold its own against outside powers. Its guarantee of liberties promised to dissolve inter-communal tensions and transform the empire into a more harmonious place.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Instead, this period became the story of the twilight struggle of the Empire.

Members of [Young Turks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Turks "Young Turks") movement who had once gone underground now established their parties.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-167"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Among them "[Committee of Union and Progress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress "Committee of Union and Progress")", and "[Freedom and Accord Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_and_Accord_Party "Freedom and Accord Party")" were major parties. On the other end of the spectrum were ethnic parties, which included [Poale Zion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_Social_Democratic_Labour_Party_in_Palestine_\(Poale_Zion\) "Jewish Social Democratic Labour Party in Palestine (Poale Zion)"), [Al-Fatat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Fatat "Al-Fatat"), and [Armenian national movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_national_movement "Armenian national movement") organised under [Armenian Revolutionary Federation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_Revolutionary_Federation "Armenian Revolutionary Federation"). Profiting from the civil strife, Austria-Hungary officially annexed [Bosnia and Herzegovina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina "Bosnia and Herzegovina") in 1908. The last of the [Ottoman censuses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Census_in_the_Ottoman_Empire "Census in the Ottoman Empire") was performed in [1914](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1914_population_statistics_for_the_Ottoman_Empire "1914 population statistics for the Ottoman Empire"). Despite [military reforms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_military_reforms "Ottoman military reforms") which reconstituted the [Ottoman Modern Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Modern_Army "Ottoman Modern Army"), the Empire lost its North African territories and the Dodecanese in the [Italo-Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italo-Turkish_War "Italo-Turkish War") (1911) and almost all of its European territories in the [Balkan Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkan_Wars "Balkan Wars") (1912–1913). The Empire faced continuous unrest in the years leading up to [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"), including the [31 March Incident](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/31_March_Incident "31 March Incident") and two further coups in [1912](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1912_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1912 Ottoman coup d'état") and [1913](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1913_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1913 Ottoman coup d'état").

#### World War I

Main articles: [Ottoman entry into World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_entry_into_World_War_I "Ottoman entry into World War I") and [Ottoman Empire in World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire_in_World_War_I "Ottoman Empire in World War I")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/M_113_5_amiral_Souchon_et_ses_officiers.jpg/250px-M_113_5_amiral_Souchon_et_ses_officiers.jpg)

Admiral [Wilhelm Souchon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_Souchon "Wilhelm Souchon"), who commanded the [Black Sea raid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Sea_raid "Black Sea raid") on 29 October 1914, and his officers in Ottoman naval uniforms

The Ottoman Empire entered [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I") on the side of the [Central Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers "Central Powers") and was ultimately defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-168"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Ottoman participation in the war began with the combined [German-Ottoman surprise attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Sea_Raid "Black Sea Raid") on the [Black Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Sea "Black Sea") coast of the [Russian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") on 29 October 1914. Following the attack, the Russian Empire (2 November 1914)<sup id="cite_ref-oxfordreference-timeline_169-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-oxfordreference-timeline-169"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and its allies [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Third_Republic "French Third Republic") (5 November 1914)<sup id="cite_ref-oxfordreference-timeline_169-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-oxfordreference-timeline-169"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and the [British Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") (5 November 1914)<sup id="cite_ref-oxfordreference-timeline_169-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-oxfordreference-timeline-169"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> declared war on the Ottoman Empire. Also on 5 November 1914, the British government changed the status of the [Khedivate of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khedivate_of_Egypt "Khedivate of Egypt") and [Cyprus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus_Convention "Cyprus Convention"), which were [de jure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_jure "De jure") Ottoman territories prior to the war, to [British protectorates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_protectorate "British protectorate").

The Ottomans successfully defended the [Dardanelles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dardanelles "Dardanelles") strait during the [Gallipoli campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gallipoli_campaign "Gallipoli campaign") (1915–1916) and achieved initial victories against British forces in the first two years of the [Mesopotamian campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamian_campaign "Mesopotamian campaign"), such as the [Siege of Kut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Kut "Siege of Kut") (1915–1916); but the [Arab Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Revolt "Arab Revolt") (1916–1918) turned the tide against the Ottomans in the Middle East. In the [Caucasus campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus_campaign "Caucasus campaign"), however, the Russian forces had the upper hand from the beginning, especially after the [Battle of Sarikamish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Sarikamish "Battle of Sarikamish") (1914–1915). Russian forces advanced into northeastern [Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolia "Anatolia") and controlled the major cities there until retreating from World War I with the [Treaty of Brest-Litovsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk "Treaty of Brest-Litovsk") following the [Russian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Revolution "Russian Revolution") in 1917.

##### Genocides

Main articles: [Late Ottoman genocides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Ottoman_genocides "Late Ottoman genocides"), [Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide "Armenian genocide"), [Greek genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_genocide "Greek genocide"), and [Seyfo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seyfo "Seyfo")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Column_of_deportees_walking_through_Harput_vilayet_during_the_Armenian_genocide.jpg/250px-Column_of_deportees_walking_through_Harput_vilayet_during_the_Armenian_genocide.jpg)

The [Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide "Armenian genocide") was the result of the Ottoman government's [deportation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temporary_Law_of_Deportation "Temporary Law of Deportation") and [ethnic cleansing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing "Ethnic cleansing") policies regarding its [Armenian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenians_in_the_Ottoman_Empire "Armenians in the Ottoman Empire") citizens after the [Battle of Sarikamish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Sarikamish "Battle of Sarikamish") (1914–1915) and the collapse of the [Caucasus Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus_campaign "Caucasus campaign") against the [Imperial Russian Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_Russian_Army "Imperial Russian Army") and [Armenian volunteer units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_volunteer_units "Armenian volunteer units") during [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"). An estimated 600,000<sup id="cite_ref-britannica-ag_170-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-britannica-ag-170"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> to more than 1 million,<sup id="cite_ref-britannica-ag_170-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-britannica-ag-170"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> or up to 1.5 million<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-171"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-172"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-173"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> people were killed.

In 1915 the Ottoman government and Kurdish tribes in the region started the extermination of its ethnic Armenian population, resulting in the deaths of up to 1.5 million Armenians in the [Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide "Armenian genocide").<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-174"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-175"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-176"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The genocide was carried out during and after World War I and implemented in two phases: the wholesale killing of the able-bodied male population through massacre and subjection of army conscripts to forced labour, followed by the deportation of women, children, the elderly and infirm on [death marches](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_march "Death march") leading to the [Syrian desert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_desert "Syrian desert"). Driven forward by military escorts, the deportees were deprived of food and water and subjected to periodic robbery, [rape](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rape_during_the_Armenian_Genocide "Rape during the Armenian Genocide"), and systematic massacre.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-177"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-178"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Large-scale massacres were also committed against the Empire's [Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_genocide "Greek genocide") and [Assyrian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assyrian_genocide "Assyrian genocide") minorities as part of the same campaign of ethnic cleansing.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-179"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

##### Arab Revolt

Main articles: [Middle Eastern theatre of World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Eastern_theatre_of_World_War_I "Middle Eastern theatre of World War I") and [Arab Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Revolt "Arab Revolt")

The [Arab Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Revolt "Arab Revolt") began in 1916 with British support. It turned the tide against the Ottomans on the Middle Eastern front, where they seemed to have the upper hand during the first two years of the war. On the basis of the [McMahon–Hussein Correspondence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McMahon%E2%80%93Hussein_Correspondence "McMahon–Hussein Correspondence"), an agreement between the British government and [Hussein bin Ali, Sharif of Mecca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_Sharif_of_Mecca "Hussein bin Ali, Sharif of Mecca"), the revolt was officially initiated at Mecca on 10 June 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-181"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>o<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Arab nationalist goal was to create a single unified and independent [Arab state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_state "Arab state") stretching from [Aleppo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleppo "Aleppo"), Syria, to [Aden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aden "Aden"), Yemen, which the British promised to recognise.

The [Sharifian Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharifian_Army "Sharifian Army"), led by Hussein and the [Hashemites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hashemites "Hashemites"), with military backing from the British [Egyptian Expeditionary Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_Expeditionary_Force "Egyptian Expeditionary Force"), successfully fought and expelled the Ottoman military presence from much of the [Hejaz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hejaz "Hejaz") and [Transjordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transjordan_\(region\) "Transjordan (region)"). The rebellion eventually took [Damascus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Damascus "Damascus") and set up a short-lived monarchy led by [Faisal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faisal_I_of_Iraq "Faisal I of Iraq"), a son of Hussein.

Following the terms of the 1916 [Sykes–Picot Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement "Sykes–Picot Agreement"), the British and French later partitioned the Middle East into [mandate territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate "League of Nations mandate"). There was no unified Arab state, much to Arab nationalists' anger. Palestine, Iraq, Lebanon and Syria became British and French mandates.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-182"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

##### Treaty of Sèvres and Turkish War of Independence

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Sultanvahideddin.jpg/250px-Sultanvahideddin.jpg)

[Mehmed VI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmed_VI "Mehmed VI"), the last Sultan of the Ottoman Empire, leaving the country after the abolition of the Ottoman sultanate, 17 November 1922

Defeated in World War I, the Ottoman Empire signed the [Armistice of Mudros](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice_of_Mudros "Armistice of Mudros") on 30 October 1918. [Istanbul was occupied](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupation_of_Istanbul "Occupation of Istanbul") by combined British, French, Italian, and Greek forces. In May 1919, Greece also [took control of the area around Smyrna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupation_of_Smyrna "Occupation of Smyrna") (now İzmir).

The [partition of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partition_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Partition of the Ottoman Empire") was finalized under the terms of the 1920 [Treaty of Sèvres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres "Treaty of Sèvres"). This treaty, as designed in the [Conference of London](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conference_of_London_\(1920\) "Conference of London (1920)"), allowed the Sultan to retain his position and title. Anatolia's status was problematic given the occupied forces.

A nationalist opposition arose in the [Turkish national movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_national_movement "Turkish national movement"). It won the [Turkish War of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence "Turkish War of Independence") (1919–1923) under the leadership of [Mustafa Kemal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk "Mustafa Kemal Atatürk") (later given the surname "Atatürk"). The sultanate was abolished on 1 November 1922, and the last sultan, [Mehmed VI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmed_VI "Mehmed VI") (reigned 1918–1922), left the country on 17 November 1922. The [Republic of Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") was [established](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Turkey#Republic_of_Turkey "History of Turkey") in its place on 29 October 1923, in the new capital city of [Ankara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara "Ankara"). The [caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Caliphate "Ottoman Caliphate") was abolished on 3 March 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-Ozoglu_183-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Ozoglu-183"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-184"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

## Historiographical debate on the Ottoman state

See also: [Ghaza thesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghaza_thesis "Ghaza thesis")

| Part of [a series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category:History_of_Turkey "Category:History of Turkey") on the |

| [![Turkey in Asia Minor and Transcaucasia, 1921](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/W._%26_A.K._Johnston._Asia_Minor._1911_A.jpg/250px-W._%26_A.K._Johnston._Asia_Minor._1911_A.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:W._%26_A.K._Johnston._Asia_Minor._1911_A.jpg "Turkey in Asia Minor and Transcaucasia, 1921") |

| - [v](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template:History_of_Turkey "Template:History of Turkey") - [t](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Turkey "Template talk:History of Turkey") - [e](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:History_of_Turkey "Special:EditPage/Template:History of Turkey") |

Several historians, such as British historian [Edward Gibbon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Gibbon "Edward Gibbon") and the Greek historian [Dimitri Kitsikis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dimitri_Kitsikis "Dimitri Kitsikis"), have argued that after the fall of Constantinople, the Ottoman state took over the machinery of the Byzantine (Roman) state and that the Ottoman Empire was in essence a continuation of the Byzantine Empire under a [Turkish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_people "Turkish people") [Muslim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslims "Muslims") guise.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-185"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The American historian [Speros Vryonis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speros_Vryonis "Speros Vryonis") writes that the Ottoman state centered on "a Byzantine-Balkan base with a veneer of the Turkish language and the Islamic religion".<sup id="cite_ref-Stone,_pp._86-100_186-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Stone,_pp._86-100-186"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Kitsikis and the American historian [Heath Lowry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heath_Lowry "Heath Lowry") posit that the early Ottoman state was a predatory confederacy open to both Byzantine Christians and Turkish Muslims whose primary goal was attaining booty and slaves, rather than spreading Islam, and that Islam only later became the empire's primary characteristic.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-187"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-188"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-189"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Other historians have followed the lead of the Austrian historian [Paul Wittek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Wittek "Paul Wittek"), who emphasizes the early Ottoman state's Islamic character, seeing it as a "[jihad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jihad "Jihad") state" dedicated to expanding the [Muslim world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_world "Muslim world").<sup id="cite_ref-Stone,_pp._86-100_186-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Stone,_pp._86-100-186"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Many historians led in 1937 by the Turkish historian [Mehmet Fuat Köprülü](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmet_Fuat_K%C3%B6pr%C3%BCl%C3%BC "Mehmet Fuat Köprülü") championed the [Ghaza thesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghaza_thesis "Ghaza thesis"), according to which the early Ottoman state was a continuation of the way of life of the nomadic [Turkic tribes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkic_peoples "Turkic peoples") who had come from East Asia to Anatolia via Central Asia and the Middle East on a much larger scale. They argued that the most important cultural influences on the Ottoman state came from [Persia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran "Iran").<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-190"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>175<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The British historian [Norman Stone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norman_Stone "Norman Stone") suggests many continuities between the Byzantine and Ottoman empires, such as that the *zeugarion* tax of Byzantium became the Ottoman *[Resm-i çift](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resm-i_%C3%A7ift "Resm-i çift")* tax, that the *[pronoia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pronoia "Pronoia")* land-holding system that linked the amount of land one owned with one's ability to raise cavalry became the Ottoman *[timar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timar "Timar")* system, and that the Ottoman land measurement the *[dönüm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D%C3%B6n%C3%BCm "Dönüm")* was the same as the Byzantine *[stremma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stremma "Stremma")*. Stone also argues that although Sunni Islam was the state religion, the Ottoman state supported and controlled the [Eastern Orthodox Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church "Eastern Orthodox Church"), which in return for accepting that control became the Ottoman Empire's largest land-holder. Despite the similarities, Stone argues that a crucial difference is that the land grants under the *timar* system were not hereditary at first. Even after they became inheritable, land ownership in the Ottoman Empire remained highly insecure, and the sultan revoked land grants whenever he wished. Stone argued this insecurity in land tenure strongly discouraged *[Timariots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timariot "Timariot")* from seeking long-term development of their land, and instead led them to adopt a strategy of short-term exploitation, which had deleterious effects on the Ottoman economy.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-191"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

## Government

Main article: [State organisation of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_organisation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "State organisation of the Ottoman Empire")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg/250px-Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace%2C_Istanbul_cropped.jpg/250px-Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace%2C_Istanbul_cropped.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace,_Istanbul_cropped.jpg)

[Topkapı Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace "Topkapı Palace") and [Dolmabahçe Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace "Dolmabahçe Palace") were the primary residences of the [Ottoman sultans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "List of sultans of the Ottoman Empire") in [Istanbul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul") between 1465 and 1856<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_192-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-nytimes-192"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and 1856 to 1922,<sup id="cite_ref-dolmabahcepalace_193-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-dolmabahcepalace-193"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> respectively.

Before the reforms of the 19th and 20th centuries, the [state organisation of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_organisation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "State organisation of the Ottoman Empire") was a system with two main dimensions, the military administration, and the civil administration. The Sultan was in the highest position in the system. The civil system was based on local administrative units based on the region's characteristics. The state had control over the clergy. Certain pre-Islamic Turkish traditions that had survived the adoption of administrative and legal practices from Islamic [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran "Iran") remained important in Ottoman administrative circles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198038_194-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198038-194"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> According to Ottoman understanding, the state's primary responsibility was to defend and extend the land of the Muslims and to ensure security and harmony within its borders in the overarching context of [orthodox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunni "Sunni") Islamic practice and dynastic sovereignty.<sup id="cite_ref-Kapucu-2008_195-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Kapucu-2008-195"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The Ottoman Empire, or as a dynastic institution, the House of Osman, was unprecedented and unequaled in the Islamic world for its size and duration.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-196"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>181<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In Europe, only the [House of Habsburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Habsburg "House of Habsburg") had a similarly unbroken line of sovereigns (kings/emperors) from the same family who ruled for so long, and during the same period, between the late 13th and early 20th centuries. The Ottoman dynasty was Turkish in origin. On eleven occasions, the sultan was deposed (replaced by another sultan of the Ottoman dynasty, who were either the former sultan's brother, son or nephew) because he was perceived by his enemies as a threat to the state. There were only two attempts in Ottoman history to unseat the ruling Ottoman dynasty, both failures, which suggests a political system that for an extended period was able to manage its revolutions without unnecessary instability.<sup id="cite_ref-Kapucu-2008_195-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Kapucu-2008-195"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> As such, the last Ottoman sultan Mehmed VI (r. 1918–1922) was a [direct patrilineal (male-line) descendant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "List of sultans of the Ottoman Empire") of the first Ottoman sultan [Osman I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_I "Osman I") (d. 1323/4), which was unparalleled in both Europe (e.g., the male line of the House of Habsburg became extinct in 1740) and in the Islamic world. The primary purpose of the [Imperial Harem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_Harem "Imperial Harem") was to ensure the birth of male heirs to the Ottoman throne and secure the continuation of the direct patrilineal (male-line) power of the Ottoman sultans in the future generations.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/250px-Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg)

Ambassadors at the Topkapı Palace

The highest position in Islam, [caliph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caliphate "Caliphate"), was claimed by the sultans starting with [Selim I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selim_I "Selim I"),<sup id="cite_ref-Lambton-1995_25-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Lambton-1995-25"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> which was established as the Ottoman Caliphate. The Ottoman sultan, *[pâdişâh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Padishah "Padishah")* or "lord of kings", served as the Empire's sole regent and was considered to be the embodiment of its government, though he did not always exercise complete control. The Imperial Harem was one of the most important powers of the Ottoman court. It was ruled by the [valide sultan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valide_sultan "Valide sultan"). On occasion, the valide sultan became involved in state politics. For a time, the women of the Harem effectively controlled the state in what was termed the "[Sultanate of Women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_the_women "Sultanate of the women")". New sultans were always chosen from the sons of the previous sultan.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="this is demonstrably not true, just look at any list of sultans (September 2016)">dubious</span></a> – <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:Ottoman_Empire#Dubious" title="Talk:Ottoman Empire">discuss</a></i>]</sup> The strong educational system of the [palace school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palace_school "Palace school") was geared towards eliminating the unfit potential heirs and establishing support among the ruling elite for a successor. The palace schools, which also educated the future administrators of the state, were not a single track. First, the [Madrasa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madrasa "Madrasa") (*Medrese*) was designated for the Muslims, and educated scholars and state officials according to Islamic tradition. The financial burden of the Medrese was supported by *[vakif](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waqf "Waqf")*s, allowing children of poor families to move to higher social levels and income.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-197"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>182<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The second track was a free [boarding school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boarding_school "Boarding school") for the Christians, the *[Enderûn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ender%C3%BBn "Enderûn")*,<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-198"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>183<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> which recruited 3,000 students annually from Christian boys between eight and twenty years old from one in forty families among the communities settled in [Rumelia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rumelia "Rumelia") or the Balkans, a process known as [Devshirme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Devshirme_in_the_Ottoman_Palace_School "Devshirme in the Ottoman Palace School") (*Devşirme*).<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-199"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Devshirme falls within modern definitions of [genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genocide "Genocide").<sup id="cite_ref-a852_200-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-a852-200"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>185<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-v450_201-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-v450-201"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>186<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

Though the sultan was the supreme monarch, the sultan's political and executive authority was delegated. The politics of the state had a number of advisors and ministers gathered around a council known as [Divan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divan "Divan"). The Divan, in the years when the Ottoman state was still a *[Beylik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bey "Bey")*, was composed of the elders of the tribe. Its composition was later modified to include military officers and local elites (such as religious and political advisors). Later still, beginning in 1320, a Grand Vizier was appointed to assume certain of the sultan's responsibilities. The Grand Vizier had considerable independence from the sultan with almost unlimited powers of appointment, dismissal, and supervision. Beginning with the late 16th century, sultans withdrew from politics and the Grand Vizier became the *de facto* head of state.<sup id="cite_ref-Black-2001_202-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Black-2001-202"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>187<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg/250px-Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg)

[Yusuf Ziya Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yusuf_Ziya_Pasha "Yusuf Ziya Pasha"), Ottoman ambassador to the United States, in [Washington DC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C."), 1913

Throughout Ottoman history, there were many instances in which local governors acted independently, and even in opposition to the ruler. After the Young Turk Revolution of 1908, the Ottoman state became a constitutional monarchy. The sultan no longer had executive powers. A parliament was formed, with representatives chosen from the provinces. The representatives formed the [Imperial Government of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_Government_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Imperial Government of the Ottoman Empire").

This eclectic administration was apparent even in the diplomatic correspondence of the Empire, which was initially undertaken in the [Greek language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_language "Greek language") to the west.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-203"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>188<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The [Tughra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tughra "Tughra") were calligraphic monograms, or signatures, of the Ottoman Sultans, of which there were 35. Carved on the Sultan's seal, they bore the names of the Sultan and his father. The statement and prayer, "ever victorious", was also present in most. The earliest belonged to Orhan Gazi. The ornately stylized *Tughra* spawned a branch of Ottoman-Turkish [calligraphy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calligraphy "Calligraphy").

### Law

Main article: [Law of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Law of the Ottoman Empire")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Zibik.jpg/250px-Zibik.jpg)

An unhappy wife complaining to the [Qadi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qadi "Qadi") about her husband's [impotence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erectile_dysfunction "Erectile dysfunction"), as depicted in an Ottoman miniature. [Divorce](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divorce "Divorce") is [allowed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_and_divorce#Islam "Religion and divorce") in [Islamic law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia "Sharia") and [can be initiated by either the husband or the wife](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divorce_in_Islam "Divorce in Islam").<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-204"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>189<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The Ottoman legal system accepted the [religious law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_law "Religious law") over its subjects. At the same time the *[Qanun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qanun_\(law\) "Qanun (law)")* (or *Kanun*), dynastic law, co-existed with religious law or [Sharia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia "Sharia").<sup id="cite_ref-otmkanun_205-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-otmkanun-205"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-206"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>191<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Ottoman Empire was always organized around a system of local [jurisprudence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jurisprudence "Jurisprudence"). Legal administration in the Ottoman Empire was part of a larger scheme of balancing central and local authority.<sup id="cite_ref-Benton-2001_207-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Benton-2001-207"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Ottoman power revolved crucially around the administration of the rights to land, which gave a space for the local authority to develop the needs of the local [millet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Millet_\(Ottoman_Empire\) "Millet (Ottoman Empire)").<sup id="cite_ref-Benton-2001_207-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Benton-2001-207"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The jurisdictional complexity of the Ottoman Empire was aimed to permit the integration of culturally and religiously different groups.<sup id="cite_ref-Benton-2001_207-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Benton-2001-207"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Ottoman system had three court systems: one for Muslims, one for non-Muslims, involving appointed Jews and Christians ruling over their respective religious communities, and the "trade court". The entire system was regulated from above by means of the administrative *Qanun*, i.e., laws, a system based upon the Turkic *[Yassa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yassa "Yassa")* and *[Töre](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=T%C3%B6re_\(law\)&action=edit&redlink=1 "Töre (law) (page does not exist)")*, which were developed in the pre-Islamic era.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-208"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>193<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-209"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>194<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

These court categories were not, however, wholly exclusive; for instance, the Islamic courts, which were the Empire's primary courts, could also be used to settle a trade conflict or disputes between litigants of differing religions, and Jews and Christians often went to them to obtain a more forceful ruling on an issue. The Ottoman state tended not to interfere with non-Muslim religious law systems, despite legally having a voice to do so through local governors. The Islamic *Sharia* law system had been developed from a combination of the [Qur'an](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qur%27an "Qur'an"); the [Hadīth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hadith "Hadith"), or words of [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_in_Islam "Muhammad in Islam"); *[ijmā'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ijma "Ijma")*, or consensus of the members of the [Muslim community](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ummah "Ummah"); [qiyas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qiyas "Qiyas"), a system of analogical reasoning from earlier precedents; and local customs. Both systems were taught at the Empire's law schools, which were in [Istanbul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul") and [Bursa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bursa "Bursa").

  
The Ottoman Islamic legal system was set up differently from traditional European courts. Presiding over Islamic courts was a *Qadi*, or judge. Since the closing of the *[ijtihad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ijtihad "Ijtihad")*, or 'Gate of Interpretation', *Qadi*s throughout the Ottoman Empire focused less on legal precedent, and more with local customs and traditions in the areas that they administered.<sup id="cite_ref-Benton-2001_207-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Benton-2001-207"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, the Ottoman court system lacked an appellate structure, leading to jurisdictional case strategies where plaintiffs could take their disputes from one court system to another until they achieved a ruling that was in their favour.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png/290px-1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png)

An Ottoman trial, 1877

In the late 19th century, the Ottoman legal system saw substantial reform. This process of legal modernisation began with the [Edict of Gülhane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edict_of_G%C3%BClhane "Edict of Gülhane") of 1839.<sup id="cite_ref-review-niza_210-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-review-niza-210"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>195<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> These reforms included the "fair and public trial\[s\] of all accused regardless of religion", the creation of a system of "separate competences, religious and civil", and the validation of testimony on non-Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-int-handbook_211-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-int-handbook-211"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>196<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Specific land codes (1858), civil codes (1869–1876), and a code of civil procedure also were enacted.<sup id="cite_ref-int-handbook_211-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-int-handbook-211"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>196<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

These reforms were based heavily on French models, as indicated by the adoption of a three-tiered court system. Referred to as [Nizamiye](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nizamiye&action=edit&redlink=1 "Nizamiye (page does not exist)"), this system was extended to the local magistrate level with the final promulgation of the [Mecelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecelle "Mecelle"), a civil code that regulated marriage, divorce, alimony, will, and other matters of personal status.<sup id="cite_ref-int-handbook_211-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-int-handbook-211"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>196<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In an attempt to clarify the division of judicial competences, an administrative council laid down that religious matters were to be handled by religious courts, and statute matters were to be handled by the Nizamiye courts.<sup id="cite_ref-int-handbook_211-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-int-handbook-211"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>196<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Military

Main article: [Military of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Military of the Ottoman Empire")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/J%C3%B3zef_Brandt_-_Fight_for_a_Turkish_Standard_-_MNK_II-a-1318_-_National_Museum_Krak%C3%B3w.jpg/250px-J%C3%B3zef_Brandt_-_Fight_for_a_Turkish_Standard_-_MNK_II-a-1318_-_National_Museum_Krak%C3%B3w.jpg)

Ottoman [sipahis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sipahi "Sipahi") in battle, holding the crescent banner, by [Józef Brandt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Brandt "Józef Brandt")

The first military unit of the Ottoman State was an army that was organized by Osman I from the tribesmen inhabiting the hills of western Anatolia in the late 13th century. The military system became an intricate organization with the advance of the Empire. The Ottoman military was a complex system of recruiting and fief-holding. The main corps of the [Ottoman Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Army "Ottoman Army") included Janissary, [Sipahi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sipahi "Sipahi"), [Akıncı](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akinji "Akinji") and [Mehterân](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_military_band "Ottoman military band"). The Ottoman army was once among the most advanced fighting forces in the world, being one of the first to use muskets and cannons. The Ottoman Turks began using *[falconets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falconet_\(cannon\) "Falconet (cannon)")*, which were short but wide cannons, during the [Siege of Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Constantinople_\(1422\) "Siege of Constantinople (1422)"). The Ottoman cavalry depended on high speed and mobility rather than heavy armor, using bows and short swords on fast [Turkoman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkoman_horse "Turkoman horse") and [Arabian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_horse "Arabian horse") horses (progenitors of the [Thoroughbred](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thoroughbred#Foundation_stallions "Thoroughbred") racing horse),<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-212"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>197<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-213"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>198<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and often applied tactics similar to those of the [Mongol Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_Empire "Mongol Empire"), such as pretending to retreat while surrounding the enemy forces inside a crescent-shaped formation and then making the real attack. The Ottoman army continued to be an effective fighting force throughout the seventeenth and early eighteenth centuries,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-214"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>199<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-215"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>200<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> falling behind the empire's European rivals only during a long period of peace from 1740 to 1768.<sup id="cite_ref-AksanOW_78-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-AksanOW-78"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/The_Ertugrul_Cavalry_Regiment_crossing_the_Galata_Bridge.jpg/250px-The_Ertugrul_Cavalry_Regiment_crossing_the_Galata_Bridge.jpg)

Modernised [Ertugrul Cavalry Regiment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asakir-i_Mansure-i_Muhammediye "Asakir-i Mansure-i Muhammediye") crossing the [Galata Bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galata_Bridge "Galata Bridge") in 1901

The modernization of the Ottoman Empire in the 19th century started with the military. In 1826 Sultan Mahmud II abolished the Janissary corps and established the modern Ottoman army. He named them as the [Nizam-ı Cedid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nizam-%C4%B1_Cedid "Nizam-ı Cedid") (New Order). The Ottoman army was also the first institution to hire foreign experts and send its officers for training in western European countries.
